[۲۶۶۱) (۱۸) اگر کہا کہ میں نے ایسا کیا تو میں یہودی ہوں یا نصرانی ہوں یا مجوسی ہوں یا کافر ہوں تو ان سے قسم ہوگی۔
اگر یوں کہا کہ میں نے ایسا کیا تو میں یہودی ہوں تو اس قسم کے جملے سے قسم واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اگر ایسا کر لیا تو کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) وہ لوگ جو اللہ کے عہد کو پورا کرتے ہیں اور مضبوط کرنے کے بعد توڑتے نہیں ہیں (ب) حضرت طاؤس فرماتے ہیں کہ کوئی آدمی علی عهد الله وميثاقه یا علی عهد الله کہے تو اس سے قسم منعقد ہوگی اس کا کفارہ دینا چاہئے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا کوئی ایسی نذر مانے جس کو متعین نہ کیا ہو تو اس کا کفارہ کفارہ یمین ہے۔ کسی نے گناہ کی نذر مانی تو اس کا کفارہ کفارہ یمین ہے، کسی نے ایسی نذر مانی کہ اس کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو تو اس کا کفارہ کفارہ یمین ہے۔ اور کسی نے نذر مانی ایسی نذر کہ اس کی طاقت رکھتا ہو تو اس کو پورا کرے (د) آپ نے فرمایا نذر کا کفارہ قسم کا کفارہ ہے (ہ) حضرت إبراهيم نے فرمایا: میں قسم کھاتا ہوں، میں اللہ کی قسم کھاتا ہوں، میں گواہی دیتا ہوں، میں اللہ کے ساتھ گواہی دیتا ہوں، میں حلف اٹھاتا ہوں، میں اللہ کا حلف اٹھاتا ہوں، مجھ پر اللہ کا عہد ہے، مجھ پر اللہ کا ذمہ ہے، مجھ پر نذر ہے، مجھ پر اللہ کی نذر ہے، اگر میں ایسا کروں تو یہودی ہوں یا نصرانی ہوں یا مجوسی ہوں یا ایسا کروں تو اسلام سے بری ہوں ان تمام صورتوں میں قسم منعقد ہو گی۔ اور ان کا کفارہ ادا کرے اگر حانث ہو جائے۔ امام محمد نے فرمایا ان تمام پر ہمارا عمل ہے۔
اوپر کے اثر میں گزر چکا ہے۔ وھو یهودی وھو نصرانی کہا تو کفارہ لازم ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ثابت بن الضحاک قال قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: من حلف بملة غير ملة الإسلام كاذبا فهو كما قال (الف) (أبوداؤد شريف، باب ما جاء في الحلف بالبراءة وبملة غير الإسلام ص ۱۰۸ نمبر ۳۲۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوسرے مذاہب کی قسم کھائی تو اگر ایسا کر لیا تو ویسے ہی ہو جائے گا جیسا کہا ہے اس لئے یہ قسم کے معنی میں ہے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن خارجة بن زيد بن ثابت عن أبيه قال سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الرجل يقول: هو يهودي أو نصراني أو بري من الإسلام في اليمين يحلف عليه فيحنث قال: كفارة يمين (ب) (سنن، باب من حلف بغير الله ثم حنث أو حلف بالبراءة من الإسلام الخ ج عاشر ص ۵۴ نمبر ۱۹۸۳۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ یہودی ہونے کی قسم کھائی تو قسم منعقد ہو جائے گی۔ اسی پر مشرک اور کافر کو قیاس کر لیں کہ اگر یوں کہا کہ اگر میں نے فلاں کام نہیں کیا تو میں مشرک ہوں یا کافر ہوں تو قسم منعقد ہو جائے گی اور وہ کام نہ کرنے پر قسم کا کفارہ لازم ہوگا لیکن وہ واقعی یہودی یا نصرانی یا مشرک یا کافر نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اسلام سے انکار کرنے کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔
(18) And if he says: 'If I do such-and-such, then I am a Jew, or a Christian, or a Magian, or an idolater, or a disbeliever' then it is an oath. The verse is: 'Those who fulfill the covenant of Allah and do not break the pledge' (Surah ar-Ra'd, verse 20). In this verse, 'ahd' and 'mithaq' are used synonymously. (2) There is an athar: From Ibn Tawus from his father concerning a man who says 'Upon me is the covenant of Allah and His pledge' or 'Upon me is the covenant of Allah' – he said: It is an oath; he must expiate it. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab man halafa 'ala millatihi ghayr al-Islam, vol. 8, p. 481, no. 15979). In this athar, 'ahd' and 'mithaq' are in the meaning of an oath. If he said: 'For me is a vow to do this thing' or 'For me is a vow of Allah to do this thing' then this also becomes an oath. There is a hadith that if one takes a vow and cannot fulfill it, then its expiation is the expiation of an oath. From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever makes a vow that he does not specify, its expiation is the expiation of an oath; whoever makes a vow in disobedience, its expiation is the expiation of an oath; whoever makes a vow that he cannot fulfill, its expiation is the expiation of an oath; and whoever makes a vow that he can fulfill, let him fulfill it.' (Abu Dawood, Bab man nadhara nadhran la yutiqahu, p. 116, no. 3322; Ibn Majah, Bab man nadhara nadhran lam yusammihi, p. 305, no. 2128). This hadith indicates that if one cannot fulfill a vow, its expiation is the expiation of an oath, so a vow is in the meaning of an oath. Another hadith: From Uqbah ibn Amir who said the Messenger of Allah said: 'The expiation of a vow is the expiation of an oath.' (Abu Dawood, Bab man nadhara nadhran lam yusammihi, p. 114, no. 3323; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi kaffarat an-nadhr idha lam yusamma, p. 279, no. 1528). This hadith also indicates that the expiation of a vow is the expiation of an oath, so by 'upon me is a vow' an oath is effected. (3) There is an athar that resolves all these statements: From Ibrahim who said: 'I swear, I swear by Allah, I bear witness, I bear witness by Allah, I take an oath, I take an oath by Allah, upon me is the covenant of Allah, upon me is the guarantee of Allah, upon me is a vow, upon me is a vow of Allah, I am a Jew, I am a Christian, I am a Magian, I am free of Islam – all of this is an oath; he must expiate it if he breaks it.' Muhammad said: We take by all of this. (Kitab al-Athar, Imam Muhammad, p. 157, no. 709; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab man halafa 'ala millatihi ghayr al-Islam, vol. 8, p. 480, no. 15973). (18) If he said: 'If I do such-and-such, I am a Jew, or a Christian, or a Magian, or a disbeliever' then an oath occurs. If he said: 'If I do such-and-such, I am a Jew' then an oath is effected; if he does it, expiation becomes obligatory. Footnote: (a) Those who fulfill the covenant of Allah and do not break it after strengthening it. (b) Hadrat Tawus says that if a man says 'upon me is the covenant of Allah and His pledge' or 'upon me is the covenant of Allah', an oath is concluded and he must give expiation. (c) The Prophet said: Whoever takes an unspecified vow, its expiation is the expiation of an oath; whoever takes a sinful vow, its expiation is the expiation of an oath; whoever takes a vow he cannot fulfill, its expiation is the expiation of an oath; whoever takes a vow he can fulfill, let him fulfill it. (d) The Prophet said: The expiation of a vow is the expiation of an oath. (e) Hadrat Ibrahim said: I swear, I swear by Allah, I bear witness, I bear witness by Allah, I take an oath, I take an oath by Allah, upon me is the covenant of Allah, upon me is the guarantee of Allah, upon me is a vow, upon me is a vow of Allah, if I do so then I am a Jew, or a Christian, or a Magian, or if I do so I am free of Islam – in all these cases an oath is concluded, and he should give expiation if he breaks it. Imam Muhammad said: Our practice is upon all of these. It has passed in the previous athar that if he said 'I am a Jew' or 'I am a Christian' then expiation becomes obligatory. (2) There is a hadith: From Thabit ibn ad-Dahhak who said the Prophet said: 'Whoever swears by a religion other than Islam falsely, then he will be as he said.' (Abu Dawood, Bab ma ja'a fi al-halif bi al-bara'ah wa bi millat ghayr al-Islam, p. 108, no. 3257). This hadith indicates that if one swears by other religions and does the act, he becomes as he said, so it is in the meaning of an oath. (3) There is an athar: From Kharijah ibn Zaid ibn Thabit from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah was asked about a man who says: 'I am a Jew, or a Christian, or free of Islam' in an oath that he swears and then breaks it. He said: 'The expiation of an oath.' (Sunan, Bab man halafa bi ghayr Allah thumma hanatha aw halafa bi al-bara'ah min al-Islam, vol. 10, p. 54, no. 19838). This athar indicates that if one swears being a Jew, an oath is concluded. By analogy, if he says 'If I do not do such-and-such, I am an idolater or a disbeliever,' an oath is concluded, and if he does not do it, expiation of an oath becomes obligatory, but he does not actually become a Jew, Christian, idolater, or disbeliever, because that only happens after denying Islam.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing that certain expressions constitute binding oaths in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins with the ruling: stating that if one says 'If I do such-and-such, I am a Jew, Christian, Magian, idolater, or disbeliever,' it is a valid oath. He supports this with Quranic verse (Surah ar-Ra'd 13:20) where 'ahd' and 'mithaq' are used synonymously, and an athar from Ibn Tawus showing that saying 'upon me is the covenant of Allah' is an oath requiring expiation. He then extends the ruling to vows (nadhr), citing multiple hadiths that the expiation of an unfulfilled vow is the expiation of an oath, thus treating vows as oaths. The key athar from Ibrahim lists numerous phrases—including swearing by Allah, bearing witness, taking oaths, and declaring oneself non-Muslim—all as oaths. Imam Muhammad endorses this. Additional hadiths on page 65 reinforce that swearing by another religion is an oath, and by analogy, calling oneself an idolater or disbeliever also forms an oath, though the person does not actually become non-Muslim; only the oath's legal consequences apply.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): A binding oath that requires expiation (kaffarah) if broken.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to do an act; if unfulfilled, its expiation is the same as that of an oath.
عهد (ahd): Covenant or promise; used synonymously with mithaq and considered an oath in this context.
ميثاق (mithaq): Pledge or covenant; synonymous with ahd and treated as an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following statements is NOT considered an oath (yamin) based on the passage?
A) 'If I do X, I am a Jew.'
B) 'Upon me is the covenant of Allah that I will do X.'
C) 'I swear by Allah to do X.'
D) 'If I do X, I will have wronged my family.'

Key Takeaway
Phrases implying non-Muslim affiliation or vows are binding oaths in Hanafi fiqh; breaking them requires kaffarah yamin without affecting one's actual religion.

Phrases That Do Not Constitute an Oath: Allah's Wrath and Acts of Sin
Rulings on expressions that are not considered oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify expressions that do not constitute a binding oath in Hanafi fiqh and explain why no kaffarah is required based on the distinction between attributes of essence and action.

Core Idea
Swearing by Allah's attributes of action does not create a binding oath.

In Hanafi fiqh, an oath must be sworn by Allah's essence or an essential attribute. Expressions like 'upon me is Allah's wrath' or conditional self-declarations of sin are not considered oaths—even though they invoke serious consequences. This lesson examines the proofs and reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expressions under discussion
The passage discusses two categories: (1) saying 'upon me is Allah's wrath/displeasure,' and (2) saying 'if I do X, I am a fornicator/wine-drinker/usurer.' Recognize that these are conditional statements.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
For each expression, the ruling is 'not an oath' (laysa bi-halif). No kaffarah is required upon occurrence of the condition. The basis is that these phrases do not invoke Allah's essence or essential attribute (sifāt dhātiyya).
3
Analyze the first proof: Hadith limiting oaths
The hadith 'Whoever swears, let him swear by Allah or remain silent' is cited. It shows that valid oaths must be by Allah; invoking wrath or sin is not swearing by Allah, so no oath is formed.
This is a dalīl from Sunnah ahad, with qaṭ‘ī thubūt but ẓannī dalāla.
4
Analyze the second proof: Athar from early scholars
The athar from ‘Aṭā’, Ṭāwūs, and Mujāhid explicitly states that there is no kaffāra for saying 'upon me is Allah's wrath'; the statement is 'more severe'—i.e., a sin, not an oath. This shows the phrase is legally ineffective as an oath.
This is a qawl ṣaḥābī, ẓannī al-thubūt wa al-dalāla.
5
Apply the distinction between sifāt dhātiyya and fi‘liyya
Allah's wrath (ghaḍab) is an attribute of action, not essence. Swearing by it is like swearing by creation—not valid. Similarly, declaring oneself a sinner is a form of witnessing or curse, not an oath by Allah.
This distinction is specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۶۲] (۱۹) وان قال فعلی غضب الله او سخطه فليس بحالف. یوں کہا کہ اگر میں نے فلاں کام نہیں کی تو مجھ پر اللہ غضب ہو یا اللہ کا غصہ ہو تو اس سے قسم منعقد نہیں ہوگی۔ اللہ کا غضب صفت فعلی ہے صفت ذاتی نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے ذریعہ قسم منعقد نہیں ہوگی (۲) یہ جملہ اپنے اوپر ایک قسم کی بددعا ہے۔ اللہ کی ذات یا صفت ذاتی کے ساتھ قسم کھانا نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے قسم منعقد نہیں ہوگی (۳) اوپر حدیث گزری کہ اللہ کے ساتھ قسم کھائے یا چپ رہے۔ من كان حالفا فليحلف بالله او ليصمت (ج) (بخاری شریف، نمبر ۶۶۴۶ مسلم شریف، نمبر ۱۶۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ یا تو اللہ کی قسم کھاؤ یا چپ رہو۔ اور اوپر کا جملہ چونکہ بد دعا ہے اللہ کی ذات یا اس کی ذاتی صفت کے ساتھ قسم کھانا نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے قسم منعقد نہیں ہوگی (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عطاء وطاؤس ومجاهد في الرجل يقول على غضب الله قالوا ليس عليه كفارة. هو أشد من ذلك (و) (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة ۹۵ من قال على غضب الله ج ثالث ص ۱۱۴ نمبر ۱۲۶۱۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ علی غضب اللہ سے قسم منعقد نہیں ہوگی۔
[۲۶۷۳] (۲۰) و كذلک ان قال ان فعلت كذا فانا زان او شارب خمر او آكل ربوا فليس بحالف. ایسے ہی اگر کہا کہ اگر میں ایسا کروں تو میں زنا کار ہوں یا شراب پینے والا ہوں یا سور کھانے والا ہوں تو قسم کھانے والا نہیں۔
(19) And if he says 'Upon me is the wrath of Allah' or 'His displeasure', then he is not an oath-maker. If he says 'If I do not do such-and-such, then upon me is Allah's wrath' or 'Allah's anger', then an oath is not concluded by this. Allah's wrath is an attribute of action, not an attribute of essence, so an oath is not concluded by it. This phrase is a form of curse upon oneself. Swearing by Allah's essence or essential attribute is not done, so an oath is not concluded. The hadith has passed: 'Whoever swears, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.' (Bukhari, no. 6646; Muslim, no. 1646). In this hadith, either swear by Allah or be silent. And since the above phrase is a curse, it is not swearing by Allah's essence or essential attribute, so an oath is not concluded. There is an athar: Ata, Tawus, and Mujahid concerning a man who says 'upon me is Allah's wrath' – they said: There is no expiation upon him; it is more severe than that. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 95, man qala 'ala ghadab Allah, vol. 3, p. 114, no. 12615). From this athar, it is known that 'upon me is Allah's wrath' does not conclude an oath. (20) Similarly, if he says 'If I do such-and-such, then I am a fornicator, or a wine-drinker, or an usurer', then he is not an oath-maker. Similarly, if he says 'If I do such-and-such, then I am a fornicator, or a wine-drinker, or a pork-eater', then he is not an oath-maker.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings with proofs that certain expressions do not constitute binding oaths. The first ruling (19): saying 'upon me is Allah's wrath or His displeasure' does not form an oath. The author provides multiple reasons: Allah's wrath is an attribute of action (sifat fi'liyya), not an attribute of essence; the phrase is a curse, not an invocation of Allah's name; a hadith instructs swearing only by Allah or remaining silent; and an athar from Ata, Tawus, and Mujahid confirms that no expiation is due, calling it 'more severe' (i.e., it may incur divine displeasure but not a legal oath). The second ruling (20): similarly, conditional statements like 'if I do that, I am a fornicator, wine-drinker, or usurer' do not create oaths. Although these are sins, the statements are not considered oaths because they do not invoke Allah's name or attributes. The rulings are based on istihsan and the principle that oaths require explicit reference to Allah or His essence.

Key Terms
غضب (ghadab): Allah's wrath; an attribute of action, not essence, so swearing by it is not a valid oath.
سخط (sakht): Displeasure; similar to ghadab, an attribute of action.
زان (zan): A fornicator; declaring oneself a fornicator as a condition does not constitute an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person says 'If I eat this, then upon me is Allah's wrath,' and then eats, what is the ruling?
A) He has broken an oath and must perform kaffarah.
B) No oath is concluded, and no kaffarah is required.
C) He becomes sinful because of the curse, but no kaffarah.
D) He must repeat his statement as an oath.

Key Takeaway
Expressions that invoke Allah's attributes of action or declare oneself a sinner do not constitute binding oaths; no kaffarah is required.

Oaths by Non-Islamic Creeds
Ruling on swearing to be Jew/Christian etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on swearing by a non-Islamic creed and apply the proofs from hadith and athar to determine that kaffarah is wajib.

Core Idea
Swearing by another religion is a valid oath; breaking it requires kaffarah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on oaths that involve invoking a religion other than Islam. Many assume such expressions are meaningless or even apostasy, but the hadith and athar show they are binding oaths. We'll walk through the proofs and the practical implication: kaffarah is due, but the person does not actually become that religion.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: swearing by a non-Islamic creed (e.g., 'I am a Jew') is considered a valid oath (yamin mun'aqidah).
This is the starting point.
2
Identify the proofs
The text cites two proofs: a hadith from Thabit ibn al-Dahhak and an athar from Kharijah ibn Zayd. Locate these in the source.
Both are from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the proofs indicate the ruling. The Prophet's statement 'he will be as he said' shows the oath is binding and has consequences.
The consequence is kaffarah, not actual conversion.
4
Apply the analogy (qiyas)
Note how the author extends the ruling to polytheism and disbelief by analogy: if one swears to be a polytheist, the same ruling applies.
The common illa is invoking a false creed.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Conclude: if the oath is broken, kaffarah (feeding ten poor, etc.) is wajib. The person does not actually become a Jew, Christian, or polytheist.
Actual apostasy requires renunciation of Islam.

Source Text

Kafir was an oath? [2662] (19) And if he said 'Upon me is the wrath of Allah' or 'His anger', he is not swearing. [23] (20) Similarly, if he said 'If I do such, I am a fornicator, wine drinker, or usurer' and the effect [athar] has passed regarding that. And he said 'I am a Jew' or 'I am a Christian' then expiation is obligatory. (2) In the hadith: from Thabit ibn al-Dahhak: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears by a religion other than Islam falsely, he will be as he said.' (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on swearing by disavowal and by other than Islam, p.108 no. 325). From this hadith it is understood that if one swears by other religions, if he does it, he will become as he said, therefore this is in the meaning of an oath. (3) In the effect: from Kharijah ibn Zayd ibn Thabit from his father: the Messenger of Allah was asked about a man who says 'I am a Jew or Christian or disavowed from Islam' in an oath, and he swore and then broke it. He said: 'Expiation of an oath.' (b) (Sunan, chapter on swearing by other than Allah then breaking, etc., vol.10 p.54 no.19838). In this effect, if he swears to be Jewish, the oath is binding. By analogy, consider the polytheist and disbeliever: if he says 'If I have not done such, I am a polytheist or disbeliever', then the oath is binding and if he does not do it, expiation of oath is obligatory, but he will not actually become a Jew, Christian, polytheist, or disbeliever, because that happens only after renouncing Islam.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on swearing by a religion other than Islam. The author begins by stating the ruling: if someone says 'I am a Jew' or 'I am a Christian' as an oath, the oath is valid and expiation becomes obligatory if broken. Two proofs are cited: first, a hadith from Thabit ibn al-Dahhak that the Prophet said whoever swears by a non-Islamic religion falsely will be as he said, meaning he becomes what he swore by. This indicates the severity of such an oath. Second, an athar from Kharijah ibn Zayd that the Prophet ruled expiation of an oath for one who says 'I am a Jew' etc. The author extends this by analogy to polytheism and disbelief: if one says 'If I don't do X, I am a polytheist, the oath is valid and expiation is due, but he does not actually become a polytheist unless he consciously renounces Islam. The key principle is that swearing by another religion is considered a valid oath because it involves invoking a profane substitute for Allah's name, and thus carries consequences.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath; a statement invoking Allah or something held sacred to affirm or confirm something.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; prescribed penalty for breaking a valid oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'If I do not pray, I am a Jew' as an oath and then misses prayer, what is the ruling?
A) Nothing; it is a vain oath.
B) He becomes a Jew.
C) He must give kaffarah for a broken oath.
D) He must repent but no kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
Swearing by a religion other than Islam is a valid oath; breaking it requires kaffarah, but does not change one's actual religion.

Invalid Oaths: Wrath and Sinful Labels
Ruling that expressions of wrath or sin are not valid oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why expressions like 'Upon me is Allah's wrath' and 'I am a fornicator' are not valid oaths in the Hanafi school, using the distinction between essential and action attributes.

Core Idea
Expressions of Allah's wrath are invocations of an action attribute, not His essence, making them invalid oaths.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every mention of Allah constitutes a valid oath. Only swearing by Allah's essence or essential attributes (e.g., knowledge, power) creates a binding oath. Expressions that invoke Allah's wrath or attribute a sinful act to oneself are considered self-curses, not oaths. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from hadith and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of invalid expressions
The passage gives two categories: (1) swearing by Allah's wrath/anger (sifah fi'liyyah), and (2) conditional statements like 'I am a fornicator' or 'wine drinker' (self-curses). List each and note that the text explicitly says they are not oaths.
The first type involves an attribute of action; the second involves labeling oneself with a sin.
2
Understand the rationale: sifah dhatiyyah vs sifah fi'liyyah
Allah's wrath is an attribute of action (temporal), not an essential attribute (eternal). Valid oaths require invoking Allah's essence or essential attributes. Distinguish between the two categories using the text's explanation.
Essential attributes (e.g., knowledge, power) are inherent to Allah; action attributes (e.g., creating, anger) are related to His will.
3
Analyze the hadith 'man kana halifan falyahlif billah'
The hadith (Bukhari and Muslim) restricts oaths to swearing by Allah's name. Therefore, any expression that does not directly invoke Allah's essence or name is not a binding oath.
The hadith is quoted in the text: 'Whoever is an oath-taker, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.'
4
Consider the athar from Tawus, Mujahid, and 'Ata
These early scholars affirmed that saying 'ala ghadab Allah' does not require kaffarah because it is 'more severe than an oath' – meaning it is a curse, not a valid oath. This supports the Hanafi position.
The athar is cited from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Apply the principle to similar expressions
The text concludes with a principle: only oaths by Allah's essence or essential attributes, or conditional statements that imply kufr (like 'I am a Jew'), are valid. Expressions like 'I am a fornicator' are self-curses and not oaths.
This principle helps classify borderline cases: e.g., 'If I do X, I am a Christian' would be a valid oath because it invokes leaving Islam.

(c) (Bukhari no.6646, Muslim no.1646). In this hadith either swear by Allah or remain silent. And since the above sentence is a curse, not swearing by Allah's essence or His essential attribute, so the oath is not concluded. (3) In the effect: 'Ata, Tawus, and Mujahid regarding a man who says 'upon me is the wrath of Allah', they said: There is no expiation upon him. It is more severe than that.' (w) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 95, man qala 'ala ghadab Allah, vol.3 p.114 no.12615). From this effect it is known that 'ala ghadab Allah does not conclude an oath. [2673] (20) Similarly, if he said 'If I do such, I am a fornicator, wine drinker, or swine eater', he is not an oath-taker. Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: If he swears by other than the religion of Islam, he will be as he said, i.e., he will leave the religion of Islam. (b) The Prophet was asked about a man who says: If I do such, I am a Jew or Christian or disavowed from Islam, then in these oaths, the oath is concluded and upon breaking it, expiation of the oath is obligatory. (c) If you swear, swear by Allah or remain silent. (1) Hadrat Tawus and Hadrat Mujahid said: A man says 'Upon me is the wrath of Allah'. Those eminent ones said that there is no expiation upon him, because this is above an oath. [PAGE_066] ... So he is not an oath-taker. [2664] (21) The expiation of an oath is freeing a slave, in which suffices what suffices in zihar. [2665] (22) And if he wishes, he may clothe ten poor people, each one a garment, and more, and the minimum is what is permissible in it [for prayer]. ... All these sentences are also not swearing by Allah's essence or His essential attributes, but are curses upon oneself, so by them the oath is not concluded. The principle is: if there is swearing by Allah's essence or His essential attribute, or a sentence suspended upon that from which kufr emanates, like being a Jew or Christian, then by them the oath is concluded; otherwise, the oath is not concluded.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings (2662 and 2663) regarding expressions that do not constitute valid oaths. The author begins by stating that saying 'upon me is the wrath of Allah' or 'His anger' does not make one an oath-taker. The reasoning: Allah's wrath is an attribute of action (sifah fi'liyyah), not an essential attribute (sifah dhatiyyah). Swearing validly requires invoking Allah's essence or essential attributes, not actions. Additionally, such a statement is a curse (du'a'), not an oath. The hadith 'man kana halifan falyahlif billah' supports restricting oaths to Allah's name. An athar from 'Ata, Tawus, and Mujahid confirms that 'ala ghadab Allah does not require kaffarah. Similarly, (2663) saying 'if I do X, I am a fornicator, wine drinker, or swine eater' is not an oath because it expresses a sinful act, not an invocation of Allah. The author concludes with a principle: valid oaths are only those by Allah's essence or essential attributes, or conditional statements that imply kufr (like saying 'I am a Jew'), which are considered oaths because they invoke a false deity. Expressions of wrath or sinful labels are mere self-curses.

Key Terms
صفة فعلية (sifah fi'liyyah): An attribute of Allah related to His actions, like wrath, which is temporal and not inherent in His essence.
بددعا (bad du'a): A curse or imprecation against oneself, not an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does saying 'Upon me is Allah's wrath' not constitute a valid oath according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is a curse, not an oath.
B) Wrath is an attribute of action, not essential.
C) It does not invoke Allah's name directly.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Expressions invoking Allah's action attributes or self-curses are not valid oaths; only swearing by Allah's essence or essential attributes, or expressions implying kufr, are binding.

intermediate
6 min
Expiation of an Oath: Options and Conditions
Ruling on kaffarah options and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three main options for kaffarah al-yamin and identify the conditions for a valid slave and the minimum garment size.

Core Idea
A broken oath is expiated by freeing, feeding, or clothing ten poor, or fasting if unable.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri explains the kaffarah for breaking a deliberate oath, based on Quran 5:89. The author details the acceptable types of slaves and the minimum clothing requirement, linking to the conditions of zihar and prayer. Understanding these details ensures your expiation is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage begins by stating that expiation of an oath is wajib and involves freeing a slave, similar to zihar. Note the Quranic evidence (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89) that provides the three options.
The verse is quoted: '...its expiation is feeding ten poor... or clothing them, or freeing a slave...'
2
List the options for expiation
There are four options in order: freeing a slave, feeding ten poor, clothing ten poor, and fasting three days if one cannot afford the first three. The first three are primary; fasting is a fallback.
The text mentions freeing first, then clothing, but the verse lists feeding before clothing. The Hanafi order is sequential by ability.
3
Examine the conditions for the slave
The slave can be Muslim or non-Muslim, male or female, adult or child, but must not be blind or missing both hands or both feet. Any defect that eliminates human utility invalidates the slave.
This contrasts with kaffarah for killing, where a believing (Muslim) slave is required.
4
Examine the conditions for clothing
Each of the ten poor must receive a garment that is sufficient for prayer, i.e., covering from navel to knees for a man. Giving more is permissible but the minimum is defined by the prayer covering.
The author cites an athar from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari who gave ten garments, each from waist to hip.
5
Confirm the proof sources
The primary proof is Quran 5:89 (qat'i thubut and dalala). The conditions for slaves are derived from the same rules as zihar, and the clothing condition is supported by a narration from a Companion.
The passage references the book of Zihar for proofs about acceptable slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۶۴] (۲۱) و كفارة اليمين عتق رقبة يجزئ فيها ما يجزئ في الظهار.
كفارہ ظہار میں مسلمان غلام ، کافر، مذکر مؤنث، چھوٹا بڑا ان سب غلاموں سے کفارہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے۔ کفارہ قتل کی طرح مومن ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح کفارہ قسم میں بھی مسلمان کا فر، مذکر مؤنث ، چھوٹا بڑا غلام کافی ہیں۔ البتہ اندھا یا دونوں ہاتھ یا دونوں پاؤں کٹے ہوئے کافی نہیں ہے۔ یعنی ایسا نقصان جس سے منفعت انسانیت ختم ہو گئی ہو ایسا غلام کافی نہیں ہے۔ ان سب کے دلائل کتاب الظہار میں گزر گئے۔ كفارہ قسم کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ لايو أخذكم الله باللغو فى ايمانكم ولكن يواخذكم بما عقدتم الايمان فكفارته اطعام
عشرة مساكين من اوسط ما تطعمون اهليكم او كسوتهم او تحرير رقبة فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة ايام ذلك كفارة ايمانكم اذا حلفتم (الف) ( آیت ۸۹ سورة المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں نا ام آزاد کرنے یا دس مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانا یا دس مسکینوں کو کپڑا پہنانا اور وہ نہ ہو سکے تو تین روزے رکھنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔
[۲۶۶۵] (۲۲) وان شاء كسا عشرة مساكين كل واحد ثوبا فمازاد و ادناه ما يجوز فيه الصلوة. اگر غلام آزاد نہیں کرنا چاہتا ہے تو دس مسکینوں کو کپڑا پہنا دے۔ ہر ایک کو ایک ایک کپڑا دے دے اور اس سے زیادہ دے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ وہ ایک کپڑا کم سے کم اتنا بڑا ہو کہ مرد کی نماز اس کپڑے میں ادا ہو جائے یعنی کمر سے گھٹنے تک چوڑا ہو۔ کیونکہ نماز میں مرد کو ناف سے گھٹنے تک چھپانا ضروری ہے۔ اور اتنا کپڑا نماز کے لئے کافی ہے تو اتنا ہی کپڑا کفارے میں دے دینا کافی ہوگا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی موسی الاشعرى انه حلف فاعطى عشرة مساكين عشرة اثواب لكل مسكين ثوبا من مقعد هجر (ب) (سنن لليبقى ، باب ما تجرى من الكسوة في الكفارة ج عاشر ص ۹۷ نمبر ۱۹۹۸۱ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الطعام عشرة مساکین او کسو تم ج ثامن
[2664] (21) The expiation of an oath is freeing a slave, in which suffices what suffices in zihar. In zihar kaffarah, a Muslim slave, a disbeliever, male, female, small, large — all these slaves suffice. It is not necessary to be a believer as in the expiation of killing. Similarly, in expiation of an oath, Muslim, disbeliever, male, female, small, large slaves are sufficient. However, a blind slave or one with both hands or both feet cut off are not sufficient. That is, a deficiency that removes benefit from humanity — such a slave is not sufficient. The proofs for all these have passed in the book of Zihar. The proof for expiation of oath is this verse: 'Allah will not hold you accountable for your inadvertent oaths, but He will hold you accountable for your deliberate oaths; its expiation is feeding ten poor people from the average of what you feed your families, or clothing them, or freeing a slave. If one cannot find [any of these], then fasting three days. That is the expiation for your oaths when you swear.' (a) (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89). In this verse, mention is made of freeing a slave, or feeding ten poor, or clothing ten poor, and if that cannot be done, then fasting three days. [2665] (22) And if he wishes, he may clothe ten poor people, each one a garment, and more, and the minimum is what is permissible for prayer. If he does not want to free a slave, he may clothe ten poor people. Give each one a garment, and if he gives more there is no harm. That one garment should be at least large enough that a man's prayer is valid in it, i.e., from the waist to the knees wide. Because in prayer it is necessary for a man to cover from navel to knees. And such a garment suffices for prayer, so giving such a garment in expiation is sufficient. (2) There is proof in the effect: from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that he swore, then gave ten poor people ten garments, each poor person a garment from the seat [waist] to the hip? (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what suffices as clothing in expiation, vol.10 p.97 no.19981; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on feeding ten poor or clothing them, vol.8).
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage covers the details of kaffarah for a broken oath, based on Quran 5:89. The author first states the ruling (2664): the expiation is freeing a slave, with the same conditions as in zihar. This means the slave need not be Muslim; a believing slave is required only for kaffarat al-qatl. The slave must not be blind, missing both hands or both feet, or similarly defective. The proof from the book of Zihar is referenced. Then the verse is quoted, which lists three options: feeding ten poor, clothing ten poor, or freeing a slave. The author then elaborates on the clothing option (2665): one may clothe ten poor people, each with a garment. The garment must be sufficient for a man's prayer, covering from navel to knees (the 'awrah). An athar from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari confirms this practice: he gave ten poor people each a garment. The minimum is defined, but giving more is permissible.

Key Terms
عتق رقبة (itq raqabah): Freeing a slave; one of the options for kaffarah.
كسوة (kiswah): Clothing; providing garments to the needy as kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum size of a garment given in kaffarah for clothing ten poor?
A) A full cloak covering the whole body.
B) Enough to cover the navel to knees.
C) Any piece of cloth.
D) A garment worth at least one dirham.

Key Takeaway
The expiation of an oath has multiple options with specific conditions, derived from Quran 5:89.
